<div id="review_984857359" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/984857359" />
    <a title="Liz Barnsley" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16471876-liz-barnsley"><img alt="Liz Barnsley" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1447272680p2/16471876.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/984857359?book_show_action=true">Jul 03, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Liz Barnsley" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Liz Barnsley" href="/user/show/16471876-liz-barnsley">Liz Barnsley</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16471876-liz-barnsley?shelf=everyone-should-read-this-book">everyone-should-read-this-book</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer984857359" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10363951740620123439">So I read the final page of “Only Ever Yours” and was incoherent for about half an hour. Literally. Thats how good it was. Unbelievably believable, , compelling, utterly riveting and scary as hell when you think how much of this imaginary world could so easily be our reality given a simple twist of history or fate, I was completely undone by the whole reading experience.<br/><br/>We follow along mostly with frieda – she’s an “Eve”, a female bred for the pleasure or service of men. She is at “school” learn</span>
  <span id="freeText10363951740620123439" style="display:none">So I read the final page of “Only Ever Yours” and was incoherent for about half an hour. Literally. Thats how good it was. Unbelievably believable, , compelling, utterly riveting and scary as hell when you think how much of this imaginary world could so easily be our reality given a simple twist of history or fate, I was completely undone by the whole reading experience.<br /><br />We follow along mostly with frieda – she’s an “Eve”, a female bred for the pleasure or service of men. She is at “school” learning to be perfect, respectful, pleasing and beautiful, and hoping to be ranked in the top ten which almost guarantee’s that she will become a companion, wife to a man with the sole purpose really of bearing him sons. Each day is filled with a number of classes and activities to ensure perfection in all things – weight, skin, hair, and attitude. When Frieda’s friend Isabel starts gaining weight disproportionately, Frieda is torn between supporting her in her time of need and maintaining a distance. But Isabel is behaving strangely and all is not as it appears.<br /><br />It is really difficult to put into words the impact this book has – Ms O Neill has a unique writing style which literally pops off the page – you are drawn into this strange yet oddly familiar world – where even when there is a drug for everything, the young girls face the same issues that can be found in our world. Bulemia, anorexia, self esteem issues and peer pressure. The school environment is very similar to high school – the popular girls rule, any sign of being different is frowned upon. As the time moves ever closer for the ceremony that will see the girls move into their next life as either companion, concubine (basically prostitutes) or chastities (those who remain in school and teach the next generation) frieda’s world starts to disintigrate into madness as she struggles to maintain her worth. It is heart pounding, captivating and often hard to read.<br /><br />I am deliberately being a bit obtuse about plot details – it will shock you, enthrall you and completely absorb you during the time you are in it, but if I tell you too much of the whys and wherefores the impact will lessen. And that would not do, oh no not at all.<br /><br />This book is most definitely “The Handmaids Tale” for a new young generation – Whilst it is dark, uncompromising and utterly daunting to read as a woman, it is and should be a classic in the making. If you want a happy read, an uplifting and redemptive tale then look away now – this is stark, unrelenting and absolutely gut wrenching, yet completely fascinating and will make you consider a lot of things. If my daughter were still a teenager I would be throwing this book at her. I’m probably going to throw it at her anyway. This one will stay with me for a long time.<br /><br />Basically, just read it now. Thats all I really NEED to say.<br /><br />**Review copy received via Netgalley**</span>
  <a data-text-id="10363951740620123439" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <a title="Cora Tea Party Princess" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cora Tea Party Princess" href="/user/show/4166936-cora-tea-party-princess">Cora Tea Party Princess</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1066440379" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15750130779347543533"><b>5 Words: Beauty, power, property, friendship, freedom.</b><br/><br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/group/show/170556-ya-shot-2016' rel='nofollow noopener'>YA Shot read-a-long March 2016</a><br/><br/>I really enjoyed this book, if that's even the right word, but by the end I felt kind of deflated. I felt that, just like the characters, all hope was gone, lost.<br/><br/>This is a good book, but it's also utterly horrible.<br/><br/>It takes the very worst aspects of human nature and exaggerates them and makes everything HORRIBLE, but you can't stop reading because it's so well written and right until the end you have this tiny shr</span>
  <span id="freeText15750130779347543533" style="display:none"><b>5 Words: Beauty, power, property, friendship, freedom.</b><br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/group/show/170556-ya-shot-2016" rel="nofollow noopener">YA Shot read-a-long March 2016</a><br /><br />I really enjoyed this book, if that's even the right word, but by the end I felt kind of deflated. I felt that, just like the characters, all hope was gone, lost.<br /><br />This is a good book, but it's also utterly horrible.<br /><br />It takes the very worst aspects of human nature and exaggerates them and makes everything HORRIBLE, but you can't stop reading because it's so well written and right until the end you have this tiny shred of hope that maybe this is the beginning of change and things will get better but then your hopes are dashed and you just want to cry.<br /><br />I felt awful reading this. I felt sick. It made me think about things I didn't want to think about. It made me think the very worst of myself and I hated it.<br /><br />Back in high school, I battled with an eating disorder. I have never understood that books could be triggers until now, I haven't ever read anything that's go to me so much. Because what these girls were feeling? This is what I felt. Every day I'd mentally rip myself to shreds, just as these girls rip into each other. But I think it's good that I read this. As much as it hurt, as hard as it was, I know I am stronger for it. It reinforced that I can do this, that I can continue fighting.</span>

<div id="review_1039016453" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1039016453" />
    <a title="Elaine Mullane || At Home in Books" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/873807-elaine-mullane-at-home-in-books"><img alt="Elaine Mullane || At Home in Books" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1525361625p2/873807.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1039016453?book_show_action=true">Aug 28, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Elaine Mullane || At Home in Books" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Elaine Mullane || At Home in Books" href="/user/show/873807-elaine-mullane-at-home-in-books">Elaine Mullane || At Home in Books</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781848664159" href="/book/show/22913648-only-ever-yours">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/873807-elaine-mullane-at-home-in-books?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/873807-elaine-mullane-at-home-in-books?shelf=readwomen">readwomen</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/873807-elaine-mullane-at-home-in-books?shelf=dystopian-utopian">dystopian-utopian</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1039016453" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7314458175627572744">I first read <i>Only Ever Yours</i> when it was released in 2014. To this day, it is still my favourite work of YA dystopian fiction.<br/><br/>In a world where girls are created and bred for the pleasure of men, the only important thing for the eves to do is be beautiful. frieda is in her final year of school and is being prepped to be handed off to a sixteen-year-old male Inheritant and live a life based purely out of service: to be willing and to reproduce. If she isn't good enough to be chosen, she will becom</span>
  <span id="freeText7314458175627572744" style="display:none">I first read <i>Only Ever Yours</i> when it was released in 2014. To this day, it is still my favourite work of YA dystopian fiction.<br /><br />In a world where girls are created and bred for the pleasure of men, the only important thing for the eves to do is be beautiful. frieda is in her final year of school and is being prepped to be handed off to a sixteen-year-old male Inheritant and live a life based purely out of service: to be willing and to reproduce. If she isn't good enough to be chosen, she will become either a concubine (prostitute) or a chastity (a nun-like teacher). In school, the lessons enforce the idea that beauty and perfection are paramount, as is submissiveness and obedience. The lessons the eves are subject to mimic the messages fed to and projected on girls in contemporary society: fatness is ugly; thinness is beautiful; saying no means you are frigid; saying yes means you are a slut; female friends are your competition; and being agreeable and subservient will win you a man.<br /><br />Louise O'Neill is one of my favourite writers. I read a quote somewhere before that said she "writes with a scalpel" and think it is one of the most accurate descriptions of her work. She is utterly fearless, unwilling to be phased by uncomfortable topics, and her sharp, probing prose pushes you into dark territory and makes you question the world around you. The literary techniques she employs are very clever; I particularly like in this book how she takes away the girls' power by featuring their names in lowercase. Simple but so effective.<br /><br />If you haven't read this book, I urge you to do so. It's an uncomfortable read but a tremendously important one. Louise O'Neill's work is incendiary. </span>
  <a data-text-id="7314458175627572744" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer11447126851674899096">This book appears to contain some interesting themes and messages, however the characters were 2-dimensional, plain stupid or both. frieda won the worst character category: her integrity and self-confidence are the saddest of any character I have ever read about. She appears to be infatuated with Darwin, her only hope at becoming a companion yet she has no qualms spilling his secrets to megan, who she constantly tries to please, acting little more than a leech. Her relationship with isabel isn't</span>
  <span id="freeText11447126851674899096" style="display:none">This book appears to contain some interesting themes and messages, however the characters were 2-dimensional, plain stupid or both. frieda won the worst character category: her integrity and self-confidence are the saddest of any character I have ever read about. She appears to be infatuated with Darwin, her only hope at becoming a companion yet she has no qualms spilling his secrets to megan, who she constantly tries to please, acting little more than a leech. Her relationship with isabel isn't any better: she can't decide whether she should keep liking her or scorning her, just to join in with megan's crowd. isabel appears a bit more genuine than frieda, but her character needed more development, and a more evident history of close friendship with frieda, which was just stated, not portrayed. I'm not really sure what to think of Darwin: he appears to be a bit of a loser at the end, and why he would play along frieda when he later says his father would never approve is plain mean. The storyline lacked depth and the setting was not fleshed out enough: is there a normal world outside of the School? The vapid materialism of the book was too overwhelming, and let down what could have been a good story.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11447126851674899096" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,

<span id="freeTextContainer12417659029042659314">Oh my god. It was horrible. But brilliant.<br/><br/>I loved how it felt like a dystopian, but didn't go down the typical route of a perfectly amazing girl tearing down the system. No, Frieda was so flawed and broken as a result of her society, butchering her from before she was born.   <span id="freeText12417659029042659314" style="display:none">Oh my god. It was horrible. But brilliant.<br /><br />I loved how it felt like a dystopian, but didn't go down the typical route of a perfectly amazing girl tearing down the system. No, Frieda was so flawed and broken as a result of her society, butchering her from before she was born. She wasn't strong enough (or unrealistic enough...) to be a Katniss or a Tris, which was brilliant because god, am I bored of those characters and repetitive plot lines. Frieda wasn't really likeable but you couldn't hate her, because she was a horribly destroyed product of the society into which she was created. Also, the lack of a happy ending was what really made the book for me. For Frieda, it wasn't okay and it's implied that maybe things never would be for the people in that world. This book was powerful and angry, and for me, just fantastic.<br /><br /><br />(Yes I'm aware this is more a stream of consciousness than a review but I've just finished the book and I do want to go into more detail and fix this up because I haven't even mENTIONED Isabel, and maybe soon I will. Maybe.)</span>

<div id="review_984861212" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/984861212" />
    <a title="Emma" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13484098-emma"><img alt="Emma" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1423392563p2/13484098.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/984861212?book_show_action=true">Jul 03, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emma" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emma" href="/user/show/13484098-emma">Emma</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13484098-emma?shelf=i-could-talk-about-it-all-day">i-could-talk-about-it-all-day</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13484098-emma?shelf=favorite-books">favorite-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13484098-emma?shelf=loved-it">loved-it</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13484098-emma?shelf=amazing">amazing</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13484098-emma?shelf=i-cried">i-cried</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer984861212" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16944924657458106038">O'Neill delivers a chilling, modern-day rendition of Brave New World. In true Huxley style, she presents a world where we are controlled by sex, by the lure of the American Dream twisted in the most macabre fashion into a virtual horror show. Voices whisper as the 'eves' sleep, urging them to be perfect, to be thin, to submit to the will of their buyers, their owners - men. <br/><br/>But what is truly frightening about this book is it's honestly, it's refusal to hide behind vagueness when presenting a wor</span>
  <span id="freeText16944924657458106038" style="display:none">O'Neill delivers a chilling, modern-day rendition of Brave New World. In true Huxley style, she presents a world where we are controlled by sex, by the lure of the American Dream twisted in the most macabre fashion into a virtual horror show. Voices whisper as the 'eves' sleep, urging them to be perfect, to be thin, to submit to the will of their buyers, their owners - men. <br /><br />But what is truly frightening about this book is it's honestly, it's refusal to hide behind vagueness when presenting a world that is blatantly sick. A world that echoes our own in the most heart-wrending of ways. Women are treated as objects, as the subject of over-sexed men who view their bodies as their inherent right to violate. Yet even in the midst of a world set against them, these girls claw at one another, wielding taunts and snide comments to tear each other down so that they can stand atop the rubble. <br /><br />This is dystopia in its most artful form, based on a reality that I have no trouble in believing could exist. <br /><br />I was touched by the brutal, honest handling of eating disorders, addiction, and self-harm. It felt truthful, it felt real. These girls are so focused on being perfect, on making the cut, they're willing to rip themselves to shreds in order to achieve it. Most of the time, if I'm honest, it didn't feel like this book was taking place in another world. It was not mind-bogglingly different from the world I see around me. I was struck by a sense of familiarity, because I have watched people tear themselves to pieces because they can't be the way our society demands they be. They can't get the guy, they can't find love, because love has been transformed into lust, into safety.<br /><br />This story will and should go far. People should read this and realise that the time has come for feminism to stop being the f-word. The time has come to tell little girls that they don't need to be able to count their ribs in the mirror. The time has come to abolish the female stereotype. <br /><br />The time has come to ensure that this beautiful, chilling book never becomes our reality. </span>
  <a data-text-id="16944924657458106038" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1202562703" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1202562703" />
    <a title="Natalie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13987078-natalie"><img alt="Natalie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1567292474p2/13987078.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1202562703?book_show_action=true">Feb 16, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Natalie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Natalie" href="/user/show/13987078-natalie">Natalie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1202562703" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14858318117576919321">BRUTAL HORRIFYING EYE OPENING are only a few words I have for this book this book will shock you.<br/>This book is really not what I thought it would be, it was truly terrifying as I could see parts, of this book happening in our society today. That's why it was so scary for me as it's not just make believe all of us can talk about these issues we, have in our society.<br/>This book starts of with Frieda our main character she is an eve along with her best friend isabelle.Women are not born anymore they a</span>
  <span id="freeText14858318117576919321" style="display:none">BRUTAL HORRIFYING EYE OPENING are only a few words I have for this book this book will shock you.<br />This book is really not what I thought it would be, it was truly terrifying as I could see parts, of this book happening in our society today. That's why it was so scary for me as it's not just make believe all of us can talk about these issues we, have in our society.<br />This book starts of with Frieda our main character she is an eve along with her best friend isabelle.Women are not born anymore they are genetically engineered made for the main purpose of pleasing men.Whether it be being a companion where an eve marries and has children with a man and then is terminated after her job is done as being old and aging just does not happen.Or being a concubine which is basically a prostitute or a charisty who teach eves who age and grow old. This book was truly harrowing and dark I did not expect this to go as far this book did considering it's ya. The author really did not hold back in showing how awful they all are and how easy it would be for us to go that bad. <br />Eating disorders were really shown for what they are and I'm so glad the author did not hold back.Me as an adult was horrified by how all the eves which you start to forget are girls! are told that being fat is disgusting and are all given tablets to stay at target weights and are encouraged to have eating disorders. It just felt so real and true to real life you only have to browse through the magazine's us women and men look at everyday where we are told fat is horrible being ridiculous skinny is good. <br />Also all the my face and social networking is very much like our society today this pressure all of us have to look a certain way. <br />This book is so dark Frieda and all the girls are very unlikable in this but I think they are meant to be by products of their environment and this is what we did as a society to them. By the end I felt so sad for all of them especially Frieda she goes down a very dark path you see her slowly lose her mind. It's so sad and this book really hit me and made me think mainly because I think we can all relate to this makes this so sad. <br />It's been a long time since a book has shocked me this much and made me think a lot about how we all are. For that I think this a very good book that everyone should read. There is no happy ending but it makes you think which is never a bad thing.</span>

<div id="review_1455845809" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1455845809" />
    <a title="F.R." class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1309606-f-r"><img alt="F.R." src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1544886612p2/1309606.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1455845809?book_show_action=true">Nov 30, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="F.R." class="user" itemprop="url" name="F.R." href="/user/show/1309606-f-r">F.R.</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1455845809" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14284605202225661855">In the future – after the inevitable calamity – women are no longer born, they are bred. Bred to be aesthetically pleasing to the male gaze and as compliant as possible. They are raised together in a school, learning to be approved versions of the ‘perfect’ woman, and when they turn seventeen, they are chosen to be either companions (wives), concubines or chastities (essentially nuns who will raise the next generation of perfect girls). There is no free will, the girls exist entirely to please m</span>
  <span id="freeText14284605202225661855" style="display:none">In the future – after the inevitable calamity – women are no longer born, they are bred. Bred to be aesthetically pleasing to the male gaze and as compliant as possible. They are raised together in a school, learning to be approved versions of the ‘perfect’ woman, and when they turn seventeen, they are chosen to be either companions (wives), concubines or chastities (essentially nuns who will raise the next generation of perfect girls). There is no free will, the girls exist entirely to please men and there can be no breaking of these rigid and concrete rules.<br /><br />Holding a mirror up to rape culture and sexism in our society, this is an angry, passionate book, which engrosses, provokes and disturbs in equal measure. A dystopian science-fiction which points a sharp and accusing finger at Western culture, so much so that one virtually finds a truism on every page. I loved it. Even as it smacked me in the side of the head to think, <i>because</i> it smacked me in the side of the head to get me to think. Rarely have I encountered a novel which I knew, well before I turned the final page, would live so long in my thoughts, dreams and nightmares.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14284605202225661855" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1300079488" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1300079488" />
    <a title="Kelly" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/732347-kelly"><img alt="Kelly" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1523129599p2/732347.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1300079488?book_show_action=true">Jun 05, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kelly" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kelly" href="/user/show/732347-kelly">Kelly</a>
      </span>

          added it




        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/732347-kelly?shelf=ya-fiction">ya-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/732347-kelly?shelf=read-in-2015">read-in-2015</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1300079488" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17327168652730087697">I love reading the shelves people have this book on: sci-fi/dystopian, contemporary, dark, horror and feminism. And the truth is, this book is every single one of those.<br/><br/>A frightening real look at a "future" where women are manufactured to become companions, concubines, or chastities (teachers of future generations). Their lives are about being thin, perfect, pretty, and the right pick for a man. It's painful to read, as it's so, so timely and unbelievably sharp in its critique of modern society </span>
  <span id="freeText17327168652730087697" style="display:none">I love reading the shelves people have this book on: sci-fi/dystopian, contemporary, dark, horror and feminism. And the truth is, this book is every single one of those.<br /><br />A frightening real look at a "future" where women are manufactured to become companions, concubines, or chastities (teachers of future generations). Their lives are about being thin, perfect, pretty, and the right pick for a man. It's painful to read, as it's so, so timely and unbelievably sharp in its critique of modern society and modern beliefs about the roles of women in society. <br /><br />More to say about this, but it's a must-read. It's powerful. My only real wish for this was that our main character freida's race had been explored a little further. It's not until most of the way we discover she has brown skin, and I wonder how much that would have impacted the bigger picture. <br /><br />A HANDMAID'S TALE for the YA set. </span>
  <a data-text-id="17327168652730087697" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('4CO/hxC7R0XkbkzDhxyExWg38itlfvKXFskboGYLxfANR+tLZtqANvDVrOwL7WryPyi/HGki9ahR5pgukEjKaQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('KdmvKQ1dgbTMxSLOp780f2uHNffpkh1MHivAl41z/nzEvfvlezxGx9h+wuErTtpIPJh4wOXOGnNZBEMZezDx5Q==')})
  }

T<\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText7824827195201329186\" style=\"display:none\">Never Let Me Go meets The Giver in this haunting debut about a cult on an isolated island, where nothing is as it seems.\n\nYears ago, just before the country was incinerated to wasteland, ten men and their families colonized an island off the coast. They built a radical society of ancestor worship, controlled breeding, and the strict rationing of knowledge and history. Only the Wanderers--chosen male descendants of the original ten--are allowed to cross to the wastelands, where they scavenge for detritus among the still-smoldering fires.\n\nThe daughters of these men are wives-in-training. At the first sign of puberty, they face their Summer of Fruition, a ritualistic season that drags them from adolescence to matrimony. They have children, who have children, and when they are no longer useful, they take their final draught and die. But in the summer, the younger children reign supreme. With the adults indoors and the pubescent in Fruition, the children live wildly--they fight over food and shelter, free of their fathers\' hands and their mothers\' despair. And it is at the end of one summer that little Caitlin Jacob sees something so horrifying, so contradictory to the laws of the island, that she must share it with the others.\n\nBorn leader Janey Solomon steps up to seek the truth. At seventeen years old, Janey is so unwilling to become a woman, she is slowly starving herself to death. Trying urgently now to unravel the mysteries of the island and what lies beyond, before her own demise, she attempts to lead an uprising of the girls that may be their undoing.\n\nGather The Daughters Estela sabia decorar uma casa, receber convidados e preparar banquetes, mas não estava preparada para o que aconteceu.\nSetenta anos antes, Johan Edward Jansson conhece Brigitta também em uma festa de Réveillon, em Estocolmo. Eles se casam, mudam-se para o Rio de Janeiro e constroem um castelo num lugar ermo e distante do centro, chamado Ipanema.\nNunca houve um castelo explora como essas duas festas de Ano-Novo definem a trajetória dos Jansson ao longo de 110 anos. É uma saga familiar embebida em história, construída com doses de humor, ironia e sensibilidade. A riqueza e a complexidade dos múltiplos personagens criados por Batalha permitem tratar de temas que se entrelaçam e definiram a sociedade brasileira nas últimas décadas, como o sonho da ascensão <div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer12012572656234300327">Louise O' Neill is from Clonakilty, in west Cork. After graduating with a BA in English Studies at Trinity College Dublin, she went on to complete a post-grad in Fashion Buying at DIT. Having spent a year in New York working for Kate Lanphear, the senior Style Director of ELLE magazine, she returned home to Ireland to write her first novel.<br/>She went from hanging out on set with A-list celebrities t</span>
  <span id="freeText12012572656234300327" style="display:none">Louise O' Neill is from Clonakilty, in west Cork. After graduating with a BA in English Studies at Trinity College Dublin, she went on to complete a post-grad in Fashion Buying at DIT. Having spent a year in New York working for Kate Lanphear, the senior Style Director of ELLE magazine, she returned home to Ireland to write her first novel.<br />She went from hanging out on set with A-list celebrities to spending most of her days in pyjamas while she writes, and has never been happier.<br /></span>
